  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer537421021466369936"><i>The author of <b>13 1⁄2 Lives of Captain Bluebear </b>transports us to a magical world. Optimus Yarnspinner finds himself marooned in the subterranean world of Bookholm, the City of Dreaming Books, where reading can be dangerous, where ruthless Bookhunters fight to the death.</i><br/><br/>Optimus Yarnspinner, a young writer, inherits from his beloved godfather an unpublished short story by an </span>
  <span id="freeText537421021466369936" style="display:none"><i>The author of <b>13 1⁄2 Lives of Captain Bluebear </b>transports us to a magical world. Optimus Yarnspinner finds himself marooned in the subterranean world of Bookholm, the City of Dreaming Books, where reading can be dangerous, where ruthless Bookhunters fight to the death.</i><br /><br />Optimus Yarnspinner, a young writer, inherits from his beloved godfather an unpublished short story by an unknown author. His search for the author's identity takes him to Bookholm--the so-called City of Dreaming Books. On entering its streets, our hero feels as if he has opened the door of a gigantic second-hand bookshop. His nostrils are assailed by clouds of book dust, the stimulating scent of ancient leather, and the tang of printer's ink.<br /><br />Soon, though, Yarnspinner falls into the clutches of the city's evil genius, Pfistomel Smyke, who treacherously maroons him in the labyrinthine catacombs underneath the city, where reading books can be genuinely dangerous...</span>

But this is the adult fantasy shelf?" <br/><br/>And don't be fooled <br/>by<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'd say fantasy. When I found this book at the library I thought "huh, a children's book? But this is the adult fantasy shelf?" <br /><br />And don't be fooled <br />by the pictures on the inside, this book gets dark! People (there are no humans, only fantasy creatures. But still....people) get eaten or worse.... It's not graphic really, but still somewhat spooky since most of the book takes place in a large cavern system.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8075689-rozalia?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289640452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10967720997598438966">I know this is going to sound really silly, but this is the best book I've ever read. Please don't get distracted by all the illustrations and the fact that this is a fantasy novel; it is a timeless, mindblowing, deeply moving masterpiece filled with beautiful imaginary worlds and <i> superior </i> writing. It's a beautiful novel for people who love books and adventures, for daydreamers, idealists, optimists, people who haven't lost their hope, but also for pessimists and people with depression because</span>
  <span id="freeText10967720997598438966" style="display:none">I know this is going to sound really silly, but this is the best book I've ever read. Please don't get distracted by all the illustrations and the fact that this is a fantasy novel; it is a timeless, mindblowing, deeply moving masterpiece filled with beautiful imaginary worlds and <i> superior </i> writing. It's a beautiful novel for people who love books and adventures, for daydreamers, idealists, optimists, people who haven't lost their hope, but also for pessimists and people with depression because I promise that this book will light up your world and thoughts for a while. You shouldn't underestimate the power of Walter Moers' words, he'll change your life. He has a beautiful, intelligent writing style and the story he tells (in fact, all the novels he's written about the imaginary continent Zamonia) will make you want to get cuddled up in bed with a cup of chocolate and a cinnamon roll and just enjoy every single page of this incredible reading adventure. I'm not lying when I say that Walter Moers is a genius.<br />I even filled 5 pages of my diary with quotes of this book, really. It's perfect.<br />I'll have to translate them for you guys because I wrote them down in German.<br /><br /><i> "When everything else is gone, we'll still have nature. It is almost an instinct that we leave the house and go out into the open air, outdoors, in our garden, with the leaves rustling and the stars shining down on us it gets easier to breathe - we can forget about the weight of the world on our shoulders. From the stars we came, to the stars we'll return. Life is just a journey to a place unknown."<br /><br />"That's how I felt; I was music and danced in a burning circle, high above everything. Somewhere down there was the world, was my body, were my sorrows, but all that seemed to be completely irrelevant."<br /><br />"I now understood the secret of music and knew what makes it so infinitely superior to all the other arts: its incorporeality. Once it has left an instrument it becomes its own master, a free and independent creature of sound, weightless, incorporeal and perfectly in tune with the universe."<br /><br />"We all are immediate spawns of the earth; we once were dust, someday we'll turn into mold. Without cease we pass by, a parade of life, a cortège of evanescence."<br /><br />"And I remembered my reflection in the mirror that I used to admire so much when I was a child, I remember the wish to be just like the person in the mirror looking back at me. Completely alone." </i><br /><br />If this doesn't convince you to read this book, I don't know what will.<br /><br />__________________________<br /><br />Update: Reading this book for the 5th time now. Still absolutely stunned by Walter Moers' imagination. I WANT TO LIVE IN THIS BOOK.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10967720997598438966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64891729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64891729" />
    <a title="Cecily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily"><img alt="Cecily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480285828p2/1199525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64891729?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cecily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cecily" href="/user/show/1199525-cecily">Cecily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1199525-cecily?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64891729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13840885395226679871"><b>What it Is</b><br/><br/>Walter Moers (and his excellent translator, John Brownjohn) love language, and that love permeates ever page, many times. Consequently, the book is a comic hymn to the power, beauty and fun of words, along with a more cautious love of books (which can provoke, or even be, evil). The books of the title are dreaming of being read, because that's what brings them to life.<br/><br/><b>Story and Setting</b><br/><br/>Optimus Yarnspinner comes from a city of authors and travels to Bookholm, a city of bookshops, trying </span>
  <span id="freeText13840885395226679871" style="display:none"><b>What it Is</b><br /><br />Walter Moers (and his excellent translator, John Brownjohn) love language, and that love permeates ever page, many times. Consequently, the book is a comic hymn to the power, beauty and fun of words, along with a more cautious love of books (which can provoke, or even be, evil). The books of the title are dreaming of being read, because that's what brings them to life.<br /><br /><b>Story and Setting</b><br /><br />Optimus Yarnspinner comes from a city of authors and travels to Bookholm, a city of bookshops, trying to trace the author of the most perfectly written piece of writing he has ever encountered. (The fact he is a dinosaur is oddly irrelevant.)<br /><br />Bookholm turns out to be a dangerous place, especially once he enters the enormous laryrinthian catacombs under the city. The sheer variety of bizarre creatures and experiences is startling, unless you're already familiar with Moers' work. <br /><br /><b>Weird Words and Ideas</b><br /><br />A random collection of some of my favourite words and ideas: <br /><br />* Bookshops are so specialised they include one for novels with insect protagonists, one for dwarves with blond beards and another for half-finished books.<br /><br />* The "primal note" is the first officially recognised note and the basis for all Zamonian music.<br /><br />* The acoustic alchemy of trombophones can induce mass hallucination and hypnosis. <br /><br />* Booklings are little creatures each of whom memorises and takes on the character of one author (a little like Farenheit 451).<br /><br />* Even the street entertainment and food are book-themed (juggling with books and book-shaped pastries); dancing with shadows is an antidote to loneliness.<br /><br />* Boring books include Chimney-Sweeping for Advanced Students by Darko Lum, How to Comb a Chicken and An Encyclopedia of Wood Planing.<br /><br />* Hair raising books include Where the Mummy Sings by Omar ben Shokka, A Handful of Staring Eyes by the Weirdwater Sisters and Skeletons in the Reeds by Hallucinea Krewel.<br /><br />* Allegedly archaic words include spinking (speaking and stinking of garlic), ambivaliguous (when you can't make up your mind) and an abcedist is someone obsessed with putting things in alphabetical order (and not to be confused with a zyxedist).<br /><br /><b>Anagrams of the Famous</b><br /><br />I noticed the quirky names, but was oblivious to the fact that many are anagrams of famous people, such as: Asdrel Chickens (Charles Dickens), Aliesha Wimperslake (William Shakespeare) and Trebor Snurb (Robert Burns).<br /><br />More here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_City_of_Dreaming_Books#Wordplay">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_City...</a><br /><br /><b>But</b><br /><br />But it's not all perfect. There is a clichéd moment when a baddie explains his evil plan (a la James Bond etc) and when Yarnspinner eventually finds the author, he (the author) speaks in a rather simple and banal way, which is strange.<br /><br />Another problem is that much as I enjoyed it, this book feels too long. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23455267" rel="nofollow noopener">The 13½ Lives of Captain Bluebear</a> was a similar length, set in a similar world, but that story was more episodic, so it worked better. Nevertheless the language, wonderful line drawings and sheer humour and exhuberance still make it an enjoyable romp.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13840885395226679871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_30651094" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30651094" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30651094?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585678990" href="/book/show/1707509.The_City_of_Dreaming_Books">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">book lovers and authors ready for an odd, imaginative adventure with a dinosaur narrator!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=tyler-and-kate-bookclub">tyler-and-kate-bookclub</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30651094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12551185258537312111">I reached the end of this tale with such mixed feelings. There were times when I felt that the book would never end and I was so very bored. There were other times when I drank up every word as if it were ambrosia, and I wanted the spirit of the book to shine through my every waking hour. Overall, the outstanding moments of imagination and muse far outweighed the plodding aspects of yet another odd-and-dangerous creature encounter or one more night (or was it day? one can never really tell) in t</span>
  <span id="freeText12551185258537312111" style="display:none">I reached the end of this tale with such mixed feelings. There were times when I felt that the book would never end and I was so very bored. There were other times when I drank up every word as if it were ambrosia, and I wanted the spirit of the book to shine through my every waking hour. Overall, the outstanding moments of imagination and muse far outweighed the plodding aspects of yet another odd-and-dangerous creature encounter or one more night (or was it day? one can never really tell) in the book catacombs.<br /><br />I'm afraid a large part of my "boredom" with segments of the book stems from the fact I could never feel quite chummy with our narrator-protagonist. The ambivalence I felt toward him certainly lessened my interest in his various adventures and trials. Also, I was not a big fan of the violence and gore and "scary" creatures--granted, these were all very much in PG-13 style, but still, not my cup of tea. I discovered that "City of Dreaming Books" was not a good book to go off to dreamland with, let me tell you! These points may not be faults of the book, but rather of my not being the perfect match for the book. (I should note that my husband was, I think, a far bigger fan of it than I was.)<br /><br />That said, there are so many chapters in this book that are rich in vivid and marvelous imagination! Anyone who loves book should at least give it a try! The story takes place in Bookholm, a land where books and authors are valued above everything else. The "fantasy" element includes not only the odd-creepy creatures, but some very adorable book-loving ones, and the fact that books have been made into more than just paper and ink. There are some dangerous books that can actually kill you! Adventure books that come with a bandanna so you can wipe your brow when you start sweating from the suspense. Books with rare perfumes. Books that actually come to life. And behind all this is some great mysteries: Who wrote the manuscript that was bequeathed to our dinosaur-protagonist by his authorial godfather and is probably the most outstanding book ever written? Is the Orm (said to give inspiration to authors) real? And is the Shadow King that inhabits the book catacombs friend or foe?<br /><br />This story is also highly recommended for anyone who loves to write. Not since L. M. Montgomery's "Emily" series have I found a story that speaks to deeply to the spirit of authors. <br /><br />All in all, I have fond feelings as I reflect back on the tale, though I tend to focus on my favorite aspects and ignore the parts that bored me! :-)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12551185258537312111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review30651094">

<div id="review_117441234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117441234" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1931718-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326569795p2/1931718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117441234?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/1931718-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789089180117" href="/book/show/6703129-de-stad-van-de-dromende-boeken">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=stars5">stars5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=wishlist-print">wishlist-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1931718-jan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117441234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7196766841738853204">The City of Dreaming Books by German author Walter Moers is one of my all time favorite books. Since the original is written in German, and my German knowledge is minimal, I read the Dutch translation. I tried to look up all the names from the English translation, so everything should be clear, but translations in different languages can always be confusing.<br/><br/><br/><b>The Story</b><br/><br/>The City of Dreaming Books tells the tale of Optimus Yarnspinner, an aspiring writer, who inherits his godfather’s possessions and </span>
  <span id="freeText7196766841738853204" style="display:none">The City of Dreaming Books by German author Walter Moers is one of my all time favorite books. Since the original is written in German, and my German knowledge is minimal, I read the Dutch translation. I tried to look up all the names from the English translation, so everything should be clear, but translations in different languages can always be confusing.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br /><br />The City of Dreaming Books tells the tale of Optimus Yarnspinner, an aspiring writer, who inherits his godfather’s possessions and finds a manuscript that turns out to be the perfect story. He embarks on a journey to Bookholm, a city entirely filled with bookshops, where books dream to be bought, to find the anonymous author of the story. When he arrives, the city rises above all his expectations.<br /><br />The shops, the writers — it’s all a dream come true, but soon he finds out it isn’t as perfect as he first thought. Beneath the city is a gigantic labyrinth, filled with old and valuable books, and many dangers, like the violent and merciless book hunters, the Toxicotomes – books that are death traps – and the mysterious but evil Shadow King. Optimus gets manipulated into the labyrinth, and has to face all these dangers and more to find his way up again.<br /><br /><b>The World</b><br /><br />The story takes place in Zamonia, the same setting as two other – translated – books by Moers: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62033.Rumo_And_His_Miraculous_Adventures__Zamonia__2_" title="Rumo And His Miraculous Adventures (Zamonia #2) by Walter Moers" rel="nofollow noopener">Rumo: And His Miraculous Adventures</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62032.The_13_1_2_Lives_of_Captain_Bluebear__Zamonia__1_" title="The 13 1/2 Lives of Captain Bluebear (Zamonia #1) by Walter Moers" rel="nofollow noopener">The 13 1/2 Lives of Captain Bluebear</a>. Both are equally awesome, and I often pick Rumo as my favorite instead of Dreaming Books, because it’s so hard to choose. The world of Zamonia is filled with crazy animals, strange lifeforms and bizarre geographic evolutions. This is fantasy like no other has been written. It might even be a whole new genre. Everything is original and unexpected, though often strange and bizarre. The illustrations are amazing, and add a whole new layer to the stories.<br /><br />At first sight, the writing style, world setting and illustrations seem to be directed at children or young adult, but these are stories only adults can truly appreciate. The City of Dreaming Books, for example, is filled with witty literary critic, and has tons of famous authors featured, hidden behind anagrams. One poor Bookling had to learn all the works of Wamilli Swordthrow* by heart, another was lucky to have to learn the collected work of Aliesha Wimperslake*. There’s also the famous Ohm, a level of writing balance and genius every author aims for, but which only few manage to claim. This makes the book a true book for booklovers, readers and writers alike, fantasy fan or not.<br /><br />Another great facet is that all the Zamonia stories intertwine on some level. Optimus is a Lindworm, a race of literary dinosaurs, but it is in Rumo that we learn how the Lindworm Vest came to its end. We learn more from the characters backgrounds in other stories. The recurring characters make you want to reread the other books after finishing one, because you discover something new every time, and want to match the new information with everything else you know.<br /><br />It is truly a world you want to visit over and over.<br /><br /><b>Back to the Book</b><br /><br />There hasn’t been a book about books that refilled me with my love of reading as this one did. There hasn’t been a Fantasy book that amazed me with it’s world so much as this one (except maybe for Rumo, but that’s the same world). There hasn’t been a book that made me buy all the other works by the author as fast as this one.<br /><br />The City of Dreaming Books is the city I’d love to live in. The books mentioned are the books I want to read. Even though it’s all fictional.<br /><br />It is truly an exceptional book, and I urge you all to read it.<br /><br /><i>(Originally published on the <a href="http://www.ergofiction.com/2010/02/the-city-of-dreaming-books-by-walter-moers/" rel="nofollow noopener">Ergofiction e-zine</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7196766841738853204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6642774356844710244">This is one of the most charming and delightful books I've ever read. <i>Highly</i> recommend to anyone who loves books, as they're really the heart of this story - both in terms of reading and writing them. I found myself smiling while reading most of this because it's just such a <i>joy.</i> This will definitely be one I need to reread as it's full of quotes I wish I'd taken the time to write down the first time but was too focused on continuing reading to do so.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1175057072790372032">This is the wittiest book I have read in a long time. A bibliophile's dream come true. It's full of wordplay and allusions to many classic works of literature, except that the references are slightly askew to fit into this novel's realm. I love that the famous authors in this story are often anagrams of well-known bards of the "real" world. The author is also kind enough to provide his own illustrations of his world. Literate dinosaurs, fearsome booklings, wicked literary agents and a Shadow Kin</span>
  <span id="freeText1175057072790372032" style="display:none">This is the wittiest book I have read in a long time. A bibliophile's dream come true. It's full of wordplay and allusions to many classic works of literature, except that the references are slightly askew to fit into this novel's realm. I love that the famous authors in this story are often anagrams of well-known bards of the "real" world. The author is also kind enough to provide his own illustrations of his world. Literate dinosaurs, fearsome booklings, wicked literary agents and a Shadow King formed of the very stuff of legends make this novel one surprise after another and keep the reader smiling (or at the very least, smirking)page after page.</span>

<div id="review_2727452896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2727452896" />
    <a title="Michelle F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44158677-michelle-f"><img alt="Michelle F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532285907p2/44158677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2727452896?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle F" href="/user/show/44158677-michelle-f">Michelle F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585678990" href="/book/show/1707509.The_City_of_Dreaming_Books">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=fun-to-read">fun-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=have-yourself-a-great-guffaw">have-yourself-a-great-guffaw</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44158677-michelle-f?shelf=anthrpomorphology">anthrpomorphology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2727452896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer487130159125619328">I want so much to write a perfect review for this ridiculous novel because it is truly magical. I've not been this joyously captivated in a long time.<br/><br/>The City of Dreaming Books is light and silly and adventurous and <i>fun</i>. The writing is perfectly, charmingly engrossing, and the translation is amazing. I can't quite tell who the intended audience is, but it doesn't matter. It is an imaginative marvel. Indeed, even with the help of the whimsical illustrations, I had to pause and close my eyes every</span>
  <span id="freeText487130159125619328" style="display:none">I want so much to write a perfect review for this ridiculous novel because it is truly magical. I've not been this joyously captivated in a long time.<br /><br />The City of Dreaming Books is light and silly and adventurous and <i>fun</i>. The writing is perfectly, charmingly engrossing, and the translation is amazing. I can't quite tell who the intended audience is, but it doesn't matter. It is an imaginative marvel. Indeed, even with the help of the whimsical illustrations, I had to pause and close my eyes every few paragraphs just to construct Moers' inexhaustible parade of creations. I was rootling around in my own imagination with childlike glee.<br /><br />There is so much heart in this book. So very much to enjoy – from the grand journey Optimus Yarnspinner takes to hunt down the best author in the world to the smallest speculative details and wordplay. (My favourite anagrammatical story and writer in Bookholm? <i>Vaddi Flopperdice</i> by Asdrel Chickens.)<br /><br />The sheer scope of this quest tale is overwhelmingly difficult to describe, and if I try I'll get sick of my own overuse of praising adjectives. Clearly I have not touched the Orm in my composition of this review, but I can quite simply say that I loved this book. I intend to visit it again, and hunt down any sequels that have made their way into English. <br /><br />The City of the Dreaming Books is for book lovers, for writers, and for anyone who can get lost in their own head and craves a ludicrous adventure. This book has enough magic to cast its spell on you and keep you in thrall. </span>
  <a data-text-id="487130159125619328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783492045490" href="/book/show/1491133.Die_Stadt_der_Tr_umenden_B_cher">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001872901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16816002054046581332">So, this is another one of those books I initially wanted to reread in 2020 because I never wrote a proper review for it but 2020 has different plans for me, so I'm writing a review without having reread it. The last time I read this book through was 2013 (and I adored it back then) and then last year, I already tried rereading it but didn't make it past page 50... so, love that for me. <br/><br/><i>Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher</i> is a fantasy novel by Walter Moers from 2004, which plays in the fictional kin</span>
  <span id="freeText16816002054046581332" style="display:none">So, this is another one of those books I initially wanted to reread in 2020 because I never wrote a proper review for it but 2020 has different plans for me, so I'm writing a review without having reread it. The last time I read this book through was 2013 (and I adored it back then) and then last year, I already tried rereading it but didn't make it past page 50... so, love that for me. <br /><br /><i>Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher</i> is a fantasy novel by Walter Moers from 2004, which plays in the fictional kingdom of Zamonia. The main character and narrator of the novel is the Zamonian poet Hildegunst von Mythenmetz, who tells of his beginnings as a budding poet, with a focus on his adventures in the book town of Buchhaim and the catacombs below. <br /><br />I remember being absolutely sucked into the world. I loved exploring Buchhaim alongside Hildegunst. This town seemed so magical, so wonderfully bookish, too good to be true. I loved the more eerie and creepy aspects of the tale once Hildegunst got lost in the catacombs. I loved how cleverly Walter Moers intertwined his gorgeous illustrations (all in black and white) with the text and how unconventional some of his plot devices and choices for the layout of certain pages were. This book, back in the day, was an absolute revelation for me. I hadn't read anything like it ever before in my life. <br /><br /><i>Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher</i> contains a wealth of allegorical and parodistic allusions to literature and the literary world. Thus the novel first begins in the Lindwurmfeste, where an idealistic ideal of an author as a person who lives only for his art is cultivated. In stark contrast to this is then the hustle and bustle in Buchhaim, which is primarily characterized by consumerism and greed for profit. In contrast to this is the idealism of the Buchlinge, who only collect books but do not want to make a profit from their valuable books.<br /><br />In the catacombs of Buchhaim Mythenmetz encounters different forms of existence, alluding in different ways to books, reading and literature: First of all, among them are the Buchlinge, friendly, dwarfish cyclopses for whom reading books is like taking in food. According to the narrative, their names are the names of famous Zamonian writers; in fact, many author's names are anagrams of famous German poets such as Johann Wolfgang von Goethe, Friedrich Hölderlin or Annette von Droste-Hülshoff. Other forms of existence are the living books and the Shadow King or homunculus, who turns out to be a human being transformed by alchemy into a giant being made of paper.<br /><br />With the tale of the Orm, the all-embracing force that inspires Zamonian poets to outstanding literary achievements, Moers alludes to the cult of the genius (= a brilliant author) of the 18th century. A genius is a person who displays exceptional intellectual ability, creative productivity, universality in genres or originality, typically to a degree that is associated with the achievement of new advances in a domain of knowledge. <br /><br />The book also contains fictional words, found in most of Moers' work. Some are onomatopoeic; others are amalgamations of existing words or Indo-European roots; still others are created by the author, like "fructodism" (= the sensation experienced when squeezing an orange until it becomes soft) or ""nasodiscrepant" (= a person whose nostrils are notably different in size).<br /><br />So, as you can probably tell, <i>Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher</i> should be every booklover's dream. I'm not sure if my non-enjoyment of the beginning of this tale last year was just a fluke, or if I have indeed outgrown the whimsical and loving nature of this tale. If I actually end up hating the book upon my reread (which I'm now planning for 2021), I will be super sad. This book was created with so much love and I remember having so much love for it myself, I hope it'll be able to warm my cold little heart when I actually find the time and leisure to sit down and pick it back up again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16816002054046581332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_386646278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/386646278" />
    <a title="sj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4740396-sj"><img alt="sj" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384356482p2/4740396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/386646278?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sj" href="/user/show/4740396-sj">sj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4740396-sj?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4740396-sj?shelf=end-of-the-world-challenge">end-of-the-world-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer386646278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6607405010340115090">Review originally posted <a href='http://wp.me/p1Zgyz-PT' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>I've been trying to write a review of this book since I finished it almost a month ago, but haven't been able to find the words.  Instead of a review, you're going to get a series of thoughts.  I can't guarantee I'll make sense, but I hope at the end at least one of you will feel encouraged to pick it up.<br/><br/><em>The City of Dreaming Books</em> is the fourth book in Walter Moers' Zamonia series, but first in the Dreaming Books series.  I know, it's a little confusing, but I figur</span>
  <span id="freeText6607405010340115090" style="display:none">Review originally posted <a href="http://wp.me/p1Zgyz-PT" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br><br>I've been trying to write a review of this book since I finished it almost a month ago, but haven't been able to find the words.  Instead of a review, you're going to get a series of thoughts.  I can't guarantee I'll make sense, but I hope at the end at least one of you will feel encouraged to pick it up.<br><br><em>The City of Dreaming Books</em> is the fourth book in Walter Moers' Zamonia series, but first in the Dreaming Books series.  I know, it's a little confusing, but I figured it was a good place to start, even though I haven't read anything by this author before.<br><br>This book...I knew within the first 15-20 pages that this book would be going on my favourites shelf.  I'd been reading a bunch of crap that I didn't particularly care for, starting and setting aside for a later date things that I thought maybe I COULD like, but that I wasn't in the mood for.  AND it was towards the end of the Tolkien group read, so I was a bit burnt out on reading in general by that point.<br><br>I know, I know.  Weird, right?<br><br>Anyway, <em>The City of Dreaming Books</em> immediately had that coming home feeling (that I've talked about previously, <a title="Book Review – Second Variety" href="http://booksnobbery.wordpress.com/2012/06/15/book-review-second-variety/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">regarding the work of Philip K Dick</a>) for me.  Like it was a book that could have been written just for me.  If I were King of the World and had ALL THE AUTHORS working just for me and I could say "Nonono, I want this! And this!  And this!  No!  I don't CARE IF THAT MAKES NO SENSE, YOU WILL MAKE IT WORK!" this is the book that would have been written...and then I'd abdicate my throne and spend the rest of my life reading this book and all the others that were written especially for me.<br><br>[ahem]<br><br>Okay, so this book takes place on the fictional continent of Zamonia.  Zamonia is/was situated between North America and Europe, and is populated by fantastical creatures of every description.<br><p>
  <a href="http://zamonia.wikia.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361357i/712335._SX540_.png" alt="" width="745" height="522" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><em>This</em> story follows the adventure of Optimus Yarnspinner (whose name in the original German text was Hildegunst von Mythenmetz), a Lindworm (read: intelligent dinosaur) from Lindworm Castle.  All Lindworms are assigned an Authorial Godfather, and their godfathers teach them to read and write, as well as educate them on Zamonian Literature.  As Optimus' godfather (Dancelot Wordwright) is on his deathbed, he tells Optimus of a manuscript he once received from a young writer.  A manuscript of such unbelievable beauty and honesty that he gave up his own dreams of writing forever, because he knew there was no way he could ever come close to achieving such literary perfection.<br><br>(Did I fail to mention that books are revered in Zamonia?  Nearly everyone is an author or avid reader.  Literature is prized above all else, and the greatest authors are said to have been full of Orm, a mystical force that fills the authors in moments of almost divine inspiration.)<br><br>After reading the story his Authorial Godfather has left him, Optimus sets out for Bookholm (The City of Dreaming Books) to find the author of this masterpiece.<br><br>This all takes place in the very beginning of the story, I'm really not going to spoil anything for you.  I want you to read it, not just read what I have to say about it!<br><br>Besides, I'm afraid I'm not doing a very good job of putting my thoughts down.<br><br>If you pick this up and glance through it, you might see the whimsical illustrations the author has added and be tempted to dismiss it as children's literature.  Please don't.  While it READS like children's literature, it's more a book written for adults that still love reading the books they read as they were growing up.  I could read it to my kids, but they'd have so many questions "Well, what does THAT word mean?  What is THAT?  Wait, read that again?" that it would just go too far over their heads.<br><br>As an example, nearly every author's name in this book is an anagram of one of OUR famous authors.  I'm terrible at anagrams, but had a DELIGHTFUL time attempting to figure them out.<br><br>Is it perfect?  Probably not.  There were a few instances where I noticed strange word choices, but that could be due to the translation.  Is it something I'll read again?  Absolutely.  And again, and again, and again.  I finished and wanted to shout "WHY HAS NO ONE TOLD ME ABOUT THIS BOOK BEFORE NOW?!"  Yeah, it's been translated into English since 2007 and I only JUST discovered it.  I feel like I've been missing out.<br><br>So, now I've done my duty (heh) and passed it on.  I hope those of you that give it a chance love it as much as I did.<br><blockquote>[...] our burning desire to open a book becomes allied with the hankering for a cup of hot chocolate flavoured with cinnamon and a slice of pound cake warm from the oven. Faster! Faster!<br><p><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386835i/746519._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="556" height="444" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></p>
<br>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6607405010340115090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62905956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62905956" />
    <a title="Katri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1324025-katri"><img alt="Katri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269157990p2/1324025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62905956?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katri" href="/user/show/1324025-katri">Katri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585678990" href="/book/show/1707509.The_City_of_Dreaming_Books">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1324025-katri?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62905956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11989617783766909949">Fantastic. I'm in literary love. This was the first book by Walter Moers that I read but will definitely not be the last. I have rarely loved and adored a book as much as this one.<br/><br/>The ultimate book for any booklovers with a sense of humour and a love for good, exciting stories. "The City of Dreaming Books" tells the story of Hildegunst von Mythenmetz (called Optimus Yarnspinner in the English translation, but I read a Finnish translation which kept the original German name of the protagonist) wh</span>
  <span id="freeText11989617783766909949" style="display:none">Fantastic. I'm in literary love. This was the first book by Walter Moers that I read but will definitely not be the last. I have rarely loved and adored a book as much as this one.<br /><br />The ultimate book for any booklovers with a sense of humour and a love for good, exciting stories. "The City of Dreaming Books" tells the story of Hildegunst von Mythenmetz (called Optimus Yarnspinner in the English translation, but I read a Finnish translation which kept the original German name of the protagonist) who inherits a mysterious manuscript from his godfather and, in quest for its author, is driven into the exciting but dangerous depths of Bookholm, a city entirely devoted to books. Everything in the story revolves around books, reading and writing, and the story is written in accordance with all the rules of good storytelling so that in 500 pages the story never slows down too much but becomes more and more exciting, and at the same time the story is voluminous enough to have time for revealing much of the fantastic world of the book. There dangerous Bookhunters hunt unscrupulously for valuable books, a book-filled labyrinth under the city is also filled with unspeakable monsters, and one-eyed little Booklings deep in the labyrinth are all devoted to a single author, memorizing his or her entire work. <br /><br />The characters in the story are lovely; the protagonist is simply adorable, and easy for any book nerd to relate to, and I also love the various friends and helpers he meets during his quest, and the villains are delicious as well. Moers' imagination is truly impressive, and his love for books and good storytelling is obvious, which makes is easy for the reader to fall in love as well. The book is full of wacky humour, and it's crazy and whimsical enough that it may be dismissed as silly by people who expect novels to be Serious and Devoted To Being Great Art. But a story about a literate dinosaur's adventures is probably not meant for such people anyway, and the book it hit my sense of humour exactly. It's also partly just the wacky humour that made me love the characters and the story so much that I also cried for it. To me a book as lovable, fun and exciting as this is worth much more as art than a thousand Serious Art Novels written for critics and academics rather than a reading audience who loves a good story and sympathetic characters.<br /><br />The creatures in Zamonia all resemble some kind of animals or mythical monsters or creatures you never imagined before. Sometimes I find books with such characters annoying because it seems the author is just trying to be cutesy or trying to tell me that Also Other Creatures Than Humans Are Worth Telling Stories About (I hate being preached at), but in this case it all seems entirely natural: <i>of course</i> the protagonist is a literate dinosaur, <i>of course</i> all dinosaurs are writers, <i>of course</i> a legendary bookhunter resembles a fox, a book agent looks like a wild boar and so on, and <i>of course</i> Booklings are small cute cyclops. It's how things are in the world of the book and it doesn't seem at all forced, preachy or cutesy.<br /><br />I agree with the warning in the beginning of the story about how dangerous this book can be. I could scarcely put it down after I had started it, nearly ignoring little facts of life such as that I should eat. And after excitedly reading its 500 pages, laughing, crying and fearing through it, I remain under its spell and will no doubt have to find all of Moers' books and read them, as well as continue reading piles and piles of other books because seriously, I can't read a whole exciting novel about books and not have it wash my brain into wanting to do nothing but read, read, read, no matter how much more "useful" things there are I should do. Because really, now nothing seems as important as good books. And certainly I will have to return to the literary catacombs under Bookholm again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11989617783766909949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3193211538" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3193211538" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1188456-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482893253p2/1188456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3193211538?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/1188456-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3193211538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1770429982480201927">For those of you who have thoroughly jumped on the e-book bandwagon and can no longer remember the pleasures of books as physical objects: this one is not for you. <b>The City of Dreaming Books</b> is nothing if not a paean to bibliophilia:<br/><br/><blockquote>It's as if you've opened the door of a gigantic second-hand bookshop - as if you've stirred up a cloud of unadulterated book dust and blown the detritus from millions of mouldering volumes straight into your face. There are folks who dislike that smell and turn on th</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1770429982480201927" style="display:none">For those of you who have thoroughly jumped on the e-book bandwagon and can no longer remember the pleasures of books as physical objects: this one is not for you. <b>The City of Dreaming Books</b> is nothing if not a paean to bibliophilia:<br /><br /><blockquote>It's as if you've opened the door of a gigantic second-hand bookshop - as if you've stirred up a cloud of unadulterated book dust and blown the detritus from millions of mouldering volumes straight into your face. There are folks who dislike that smell and turn on their heel as soon as it assails their nostrils. It isn't an agreeable odour, granted. Hopelessly antiquated, it is eloquent of decay and dissolution, mildew and mortality. But it also has other associations: a hint of acidity reminiscent of lemon trees in flower; the stimulating scent of old leather; the acrid, intelligent tang of printer's ink; and, overlying all else, a reassuring aroma of wood.</blockquote><br /><br />In the town of Bookholm, people (or beings, rather) kill for books - the disreputable bookhunters who trawl the subterranean book caverns looking for the rare and unusual - and are killed by them (take your pick: trap books, toxicotomes with poisonous inks, books that hypnotize). They go into book rages in which they frantically buy any and all books within sight. They trade books, review books, memorize books, eat books...<i>ride bookshelves</i>...<br /><br />And of course, all mysteries and intrigues in this world begin and end with books, too. Young Optimus Yarnspinner arrives in Bookholm with a mysterious manuscript that, despite its prosaic subject (writer's block), is pure genius. His goals - to find its author, and perhaps to find his own voice as a writer - soon lead him deep into the bowels of the city and its secrets.<br /><br />The pace is leisurely, digressive, and chatty in an erudite and deeply weird way. It will definitely not appeal to everyone. Despite the fact that <b>The City of Dreaming Books</b> has been called YA or even children's fantasy, it is dense with literary allusions (a character named Aleisha Wimpersleake [William Shakespeare] has studied the more obscure works of one Ergor Banco [Roger Bacon]) and sly references to things that would have gone straight over my head as a teen. Poison Alley, for example, is "the notorious haunt of reviewers who plied for hire" (i.e. poisoned pen! Side note: I once considered a ghostwriting business called The Poisoned Inkwell). And comments like, "So you still can't write books [...] but you can already kill them. Are you sure you wouldn't prefer to be a literary critic?" The humor is understated and very bookish, and for all that there's plenty of action and phantasmagoria, a good deal of the focus is actually on Optimus's development as a writer and coming of age.<br /><br />Optimus is a bit of a Dr. Watson - wordy, fussy, a little slow on the uptake - and frequently has to be rescued from the situations he finds himself in. I think I enjoyed the strange but bookish settings and the digressions more than I cared about his fate, but I did find the ending entirely satisfying. <br /><br />I wouldn't have guessed this was a translation of a German text, so kudos to translator John Brownjohn. It reads beautifully. Thanks to Maya for this recommendation!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1770429982480201927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1958791973" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14277654695011366170">It is now official, I have a new favorite author and series. Having been totally blown away from Moers first two books set in the mythical lost continent of Zamonia my expectations was high for more madcap calamity in the land of living books. Tee-hee this was such an awesome read. Narrated by trepid adventurer Optimus Yarnspinner, he describes his perilous journey to find the identity of the author of a manuscript that is the most accomplished Zamonian writing ever put to paper. Traveling to Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText14277654695011366170" style="display:none">It is now official, I have a new favorite author and series. Having been totally blown away from Moers first two books set in the mythical lost continent of Zamonia my expectations was high for more madcap calamity in the land of living books. Tee-hee this was such an awesome read. Narrated by trepid adventurer Optimus Yarnspinner, he describes his perilous journey to find the identity of the author of a manuscript that is the most accomplished Zamonian writing ever put to paper. Traveling to Bookholm, that is legendarily known as The City of Dreaming Books, little does Optimus know that he is entering a land full of danger with friends and foes.<br /><br />As you may have guessed for anyone who follows my reviews, Walter Moers has captured me hook line and magical sinker. If I was going to try and describe the world of Zamonia it would probably be, think the magical weirdness of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/338705.Catherynne_M__Valente" title="Catherynne M. Valente" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherynne M. Valente</a>'s Fairyland and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>'s Discworld series injected with 100% more zaniness and creativity. The City of Dreaming Books is a literary delight with living books, cute little cyclops creatures called booklings and the mysterious one called The Shadow King. Whimsical to the max, you can tell the authors humor when he declares the fictional character <i>Hildegunst von Mythenmetz</i> as the actual author and Moers has just translated the books from Zamonian to German. If you like weirdness in your reading then look no further.</span>

<div id="review_121056489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121056489" />
    <a title="Sandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478030-sandra"><img alt="Sandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574023546p2/1478030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121056489?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra" href="/user/show/1478030-sandra">Sandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783492246880" href="/book/show/1491113.Die_Stadt_der_Tr_umenden_B_cher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=in-german">in-german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1478030-sandra?shelf=uni-inspired">uni-inspired</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121056489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6106334418334555976">Do you love reading? Do you love fantasy worlds? And do you love books? In that case, this book is for you. It's the story of a dinosaur who goes to a city where everything, and I mean everything, has to do with books. The newspaper <i>Die Welt</i> has called this a love declaration for literature, and in that, the critic was quite correct. I'm a bit hestitant to talk about the book or its fantasy world, because I don't want to spoil anything! But in short: the city of Buchhaim is a city full of books,</span>
  <span id="freeText6106334418334555976" style="display:none">Do you love reading? Do you love fantasy worlds? And do you love books? In that case, this book is for you. It's the story of a dinosaur who goes to a city where everything, and I mean everything, has to do with books. The newspaper <i>Die Welt</i> has called this a love declaration for literature, and in that, the critic was quite correct. I'm a bit hestitant to talk about the book or its fantasy world, because I don't want to spoil anything! But in short: the city of Buchhaim is a city full of books, where everyone reads and where there are hundreds of book stores. Everyone hopes to find an old book, especially those from the golden list, who are worth a fortune. These books however are usually buried underground (about 90% of Buchhaim is underground) and so Book Hunters usually go underground to look for these books: which is not entirely without danger. There are many creatures down there, none that we know of from this world, and not to mention the feud between all Book Hunters, based on the fact that they're all greedy. Hildegunst von Mythenmetz (as he's called in German), our protagonist, is a dinosaur coming to this city with a perfect manuscript in hand. He's curious as to who's written it and is looking for answers. Little does he know, that the manuscript is more dangerous than it seems..<br /><br />I must admit that the story in itself didn't really fascinate me, at least not to the same extent some other things did. It was a good story, but not what really captured my attention. What I loved most about this book, was the love for books and literature. There is love for the written word in every single sentence, every single word. The city of Buchhaim and its underground world were fascinating: both scary and really beautiful. I fell in love with both the Living Books and the Booklings, who are both wonderful creatures that I'd dearly love to have as companions. The story and the fantasy world are both good, but what carries this book is the love for everything readable. And consequently, I fell in love with the book too.<br /><br />The writing is also amazing. I don't know about translations, but the original German is so gorgeous. I have an insane love for the German language and its clear sounds, the way it tastes in your mouth and the strength it possesses. And this, this.. was just exceptional German. I can understand easily now, why my Literature Professor declared this was good literature and recommended it to all of us. It's so much more than just a fantasy novel. This book really, really is amazing and I would recommend it to every single one of you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6106334418334555976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_674904746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/674904746" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903197-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311861358p2/5903197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/674904746?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/5903197-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783492246880" href="/book/show/1491113.Die_Stadt_der_Tr_umenden_B_cher">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=deutsch">deutsch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903197-tim?shelf=walter-moers-zamonien">walter-moers-zamonien</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer674904746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15180593540438485695">Wow! Amazing! Mindblowing! A true masterpiece! I've never read anything by Walter Moers. Walter Moers was in a way recommended to me (elsewhere) last year when I was asking for German books (by German authors, of course) (Fantasy/SF/Historical Fiction - see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/recommendation_requests/51741' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> - feel free to add books), but back then I thought his books were part of a series, which one had to read in order and I didn't/don't want that, because my German isn't as fluent (yet) as my English, even though I'm at level B1.<br/><br/>Anyway, l</span>
  <span id="freeText15180593540438485695" style="display:none">Wow! Amazing! Mindblowing! A true masterpiece! I've never read anything by Walter Moers. Walter Moers was in a way recommended to me (elsewhere) last year when I was asking for German books (by German authors, of course) (Fantasy/SF/Historical Fiction - see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/recommendation_requests/51741" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> - feel free to add books), but back then I thought his books were part of a series, which one had to read in order and I didn't/don't want that, because my German isn't as fluent (yet) as my English, even though I'm at level B1.<br /><br />Anyway, last month I was walking around in the Fnac in Brussels, Belgium, to find out about their German bookshelf and mainly these were of interest to me:<br /><br />* Frank Schätzing - Limit (for 9,99 EUR): I want to read that one, but why must it be in so small print? :( The Swarm (even the hardcover version I have) also has a small print.<br />* Frank Schätzing - Die Dunkle Seite<br />* Walter Moers - Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher<br />* Walter Moers - Das Labyrinth der Träumenden Bücher (sort of follow-up of Die Stadt...)<br /><br />After careful consideration (reading the back, reading a bit of the text inside) I bought Walter Moers - Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher. It seems the books don't have to be read in order, after all. Except of course for those linked to each other, like Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher and Das Labyrinth der Träumenden Bücher.<br /><br />Yes, I read the book in German, for obvious reasons. But Die Stadt... is thus a stand-alone book and perfect by itself.<br /><br />And what a journey/voyage it has been! Prepare for an escape out of the real world. The book's main story aside (see the description on the book's page or on <a href="http://www.zamonien.de/zamonien_romane.php" rel="nofollow noopener">Zamonien.de</a>, you'll see that there are two parts: 1) Danzelots Vermächtnis, and 2) Die Katakomben von Buchhaim.<br /><br />In the first part you get to know about Hildegunst von Mythenmetz's trip from the Lindwurmfest to the famed city of Buchhaim, where everything revolves around books and selling books in the many antiquarian bookshops. Books of high value, books of lesser value, but mainly those of The Golden List were highly sought after and expensive. This part was funny, it was a very pleasant reading. Walter Moers also used many words throughout the book that I don't/didn't know yet, but when you read the sentences, the context, then it's relatively easy to know what he's talking about.<br /><br />The second part is where all the adventure takes place. And an adventure it is. Indiana Jones has nothing on Hildegunst von Mythenmetz. Add an enormous amount of imagination in terms of books, creatures living underground, living books, shadows, and anything book-related, especially the importance of the written word in the form of poetry or stories. Because that's another thing one can read every now and then: pieces of poetry, which then have an impact that very moment or later on in the story.<br /><br />Die Stadt der Träumenden Bücher is (as Die Welt stated it) a enormous declaration of love with regards to literature and reading. It's, in my opinion, a multi-layered book, not just about books and reading. It also contains elements of friendship (and enmity), trade, philosophy, how to overcome obstacles in life (e.g. at first it's easy, but when it gets hard, you have to continue - else, why did you start it anyway? - for in the end you'll be glad you persisted), and so on. Plus, an enormous dose of fun and witty stuff.<br /><br />It is an exciting book, you're encouraged to read on, to find out what will happen next, what else hides in the catacombs beneath Buchhaim. At some point, say the last 100 pages, I was having trouble reading on. My mind couldn't take it anymore and I was on the verge of holding a reading break (after finishing Die Stadt...). But as I pressed on, the joy of reading and experiencing the adventure with Hildegunst, the pleasure was rekindled with ease.<br /><br />Walter Moers has one hell of an imagination, having written a story I've never read before; using a vocabulary that makes it simply a joy to read, even if it's in German. Because, frankly, I think one should indeed read it in German. And while you may think that the drawings (made my Walter Moers himself) and the context comes across as "for children", I can assure you this is a book for adults.<br /><br />The story made me laugh on many occasions, it drew me inside to - like I said before - experience the dangers and other experiences by myself (or through my imagination). It also - near the end - made me shed a tear or two, as the unexpected twist (Buchlinge arising to the surface) took place, but also as the big friendship between the main characters ceased to exist. No, I don't want to give away too many details.<br /><br />I also like how Walter Moers gives a little sting to the book industry, by stating that much of what's coming out is in fact rubbish, mainstream stuff, easy to read and digest, brainless stuff (extremely put). That profits are made from the amount of paper sold, not the words written on that paper.<br /><br />Long story short: absolutely wonderful! One of the best stories I've ever read. Superhighly recommended!<br /><br />-----------------------------------------<br /><br />Deutsch: folgt bald.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15180593540438485695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_577447537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/577447537" />
    <a title="Lea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17194389-lea"><img alt="Lea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360742309p2/17194389.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/577447537?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea" href="/user/show/17194389-lea">Lea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783492246880" href="/book/show/1491113.Die_Stadt_der_Tr_umenden_B_cher">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer577447537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9171649636549241670">When I first saw this book, I was on a city trip to Berlin. I needed some time for myself, and had the need for an escape from my everyday student life. At first the cover awakened my attention, a book with books on it. How wonderful! (Especially if you really-really-really, are into books) and the title makes it even better.<br/>But then I wouldn’t buy it at first. Walter Moors has also written "The 13½ Lives of Captain Bluebear", and as every other German I do associate this with children’s stories</span>
  <span id="freeText9171649636549241670" style="display:none">When I first saw this book, I was on a city trip to Berlin. I needed some time for myself, and had the need for an escape from my everyday student life. At first the cover awakened my attention, a book with books on it. How wonderful! (Especially if you really-really-really, are into books) and the title makes it even better.<br />But then I wouldn’t buy it at first. Walter Moors has also written "The 13½ Lives of Captain Bluebear", and as every other German I do associate this with children’s stories. Besides this was fantasy, which I usually avoid. However the next time I passed the store I HAD to buy it. I didn’t regret it once and I was so thankful for reading it in the original language. <br /><br />The book spell-bound me and on the bus on the way home I actually laughed out loud and sometimes there was a little tear in the corner of my eye (those of you who have read the book, might recognize something here…)<br /><br />The story is about a dinosaur, who inherits a manuscript, which is so well-written that can’t rest until he has found the author of this text. He travels to “The city of dreaming books”- a city which exists based on antiquarian bookshops, where books which once have had a life, now dream of a second life while they lie in big piles and I shop windows. Everyone our protagonist asks about this manuscript closes the door, and tells him to go away, but he doesn’t want to leave until he knows the author. But only 10% percent of the city sees daylight while there is a huge network of corridors and passages underneath it, filled with old books and mysterious creatures…<br />Walter Moors’ language is fantastic, and his way of using irony is intelligent and hilarious at the same time.<br /> <br />The book turned out to be an extension from my escape from reality and it awakened my love for litterature. I am certainly going to read it again.<br /></span>

          </span>
